J_u=\\frac{J_u}{\\|J_u\\|},\r\n\\qquad\r\n\\widehat J_d=\\frac{J_d}{\\|J_d\\|}.\r\n\\]\r\n\r\nUse the canonical Freudenthal quartic\r\n\r\n\\[\r\n\\Delta\r\n=\r\n\\left(\r\n1-\\langle \\widehat J_u,\\widehat J_d\\rangle\r\n\\right)^2\r\n-\r\n4\\left(\r\nN(\\widehat J_u)\r\n+\r\nN(\\widehat J_d)\r\n-\r\n\\langle \\widehat J_u^\\#,\\widehat J_d^\\#\\rangle\r\n\\right).\r\n\\]\r\n\r\nThen add the determinant correction:\r\n\r\n\\[\r\n\\boxed{\r\n\\mathcal A_{\\text{twist}}\r\n=\r\n\\Delta\r\n-\r\n2N(\\widehat J_d).\r\n}\r\n\\]\r\n\r\nThis is invariant data only:\r\n\r\n- Freudenthal quartic \\(\\Delta\\),\r\n- Jordan cubic norm \\(N\\),\r\n- Jordan adjoint \\(J^\\#\\),\r\n- no CKM numbers.\r\n\r\n---\r\n\r\n# Why this selects \\(K\\)\r\n\r\nLet\r\n\r\n\\[\r\nK=\\kappa_1K_1+\\kappa_2K_2.\r\n\\]\r\n\r\nIn the unused vacuum plane, define the Ladders of the Octonion Associator — One-Pager\n\n**Date:** 2026-07-09 · **Full paper:** `SPECTRAL_LADDERS_PAPER.md` · **arXiv-ready note:** `THEOREM_NOTE.tex`\n\n## The finding in one sentence\n\nThe octonion associator's natural mass matrices can only have *self-similar* (geometric) spectra at one specific base per frame size — the reciprocal k-bonacci constants — and they hit them exactly: golden ratio (3 generations), tribonacci (4), tetranacci (5), pentanacci (6), with a reproducible near-miss at the terminal size 7.\n\n## Why it happened at all\n\nThe operator is $M_{ab} = \\|[u_a, u_b, H]\\|^2$: how much a triple-product of \"generation\" directions fails to associate. Because octonions are **alternative**, $[u,u,H] = 0$ — so $M$ always has a **zero diagonal**. Its entries are squared norms, so it's **nonnegative**. Zero trace + nonnegative + symmetric forces the spectrum's sign pattern (Perron–Frobenius), giving an exact **sum rule**:\n\n$$s_1 = s_2 + s_3 + \\cdots + s_n \\quad \\text{(every frame, every vacuum, no fine-tuning)}$$\n\nDemand a geometric ladder $(1, x, x^2, \\ldots)$ on top of the sum rule and the base *must* solve\n$1 = x + x^2 + \\cdots + x^{n-1}$ — for $n{=}3$, that is **the defining equation of the golden ratio**.\n\n## The scoreboard\n\n| frames $n$ | base must be | achieved | epistemic status |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| 3 | golden 0.6180340 | 0.6180340 | **theorem** (proved) |\n| 4 | tribonacci 0.5436890 | 0.5436890 | numerically exact (24/24 starts) |\n| 5 | tetranacci 0.5187901 | 0.5187901 | numerically exact (machine zero) |\n| 6 | pentanacci 0.5086604 | 0.5086604 | numerically exact (machine zero) |\n| 7 | hexanacci 0.5041383 | 0.5049 (stall @ 10⁻⁸) | **numerically excluded** (0/28 starts) |\n\n*(Rows differ in epistemic strength: one proof, three machine-precision realizations, one numerical exclusion. The golden spectrum is the unique geometric spectrum, not the unique spectrum — non-geometric spectra fill the whole sum-rule segment.)*\n\n## What it kills, and what it predicts\n\n- **Kills (exactly, not approximately):** deriving Froggatt–Nielsen / Cabibbo-type fermion mass\n  hierarchies $(1, \\lambda^2, \\lambda^4)$ from this operator class — the sum rule forbids every\n  strongly hierarchical texture at every frame size. A years-long numerical search is closed by a\n  three-line proof.\n- **Predicts:** any future mass model built on octonion-associator Gram matrices carries the rigid\n  parameter-free signature $m_1 = m_2 + m_3$ (in the sum-rule normalization). Nothing in the\n  observed fermion spectrum looks like that — an independent restatement of the obstruction.\n\n## What's genuinely open (two crisp problems)\n\n1. **Universal sum rule conjecture.** For $n \\geq 4$, matrix theory alone permits violations\n   (CFJK, SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl. 2013) — yet 0 violations in 45,000+ random frames. Why is\n   the octonionic image confined to the extreme stratum? Likely provable via $G_2$-invariance.\n2. **Hexanacci non-realizability.** At $n=7$ the search space collapses to $O(7)/G_2$ (7-dim)\n   vs 5 ladder constraints — dimension counting says it *should* fit, yet 28 independent runs\n   stall $9 \\times 10^{-4}$ high. Prove the miss or find the frame.\n\n## Caveats (earned the hard way)\n\n- Results require the **exact** algebra. A vector-part truncation of octonion multiplication\n  (innocuous-looking, used in the companion ML study) breaks alternativity and erases everything\n  above — and briefly produced a false refutation before being caught.\n- Do not over-read the golden ratio: no $E_8$, no quasicrystals, no mysticism. The mechanism is\n  antisymmetry + nonnegativity + the polynomial $1 = x + \\cdots + x^{n-1}$. That is the whole trick.\n\n**Reproduce:** `python tribonacci_test.py` (CPU, minutes). Sum-rule self-check built into\n`mechanism_test.py`. All numbers in this document trace to `RESULTS.md` Experiments 5–7.\n\n# The Octonion Associator as a Neural Inductive Bias: From Failed Flavor Physics to Bounded Geometric Priors\n\n**Abstract.** We report a negative result in flavor physics and its systematic conversion into a bounded machine-learning result. An attempt to derive Standard Model fermion mass hierarchies from the octonion associator — motivated by $E_6$ grand-unified constructions in which one fermion generation occupies the $\\mathbf{27}$ — failed in a specific way: the singular-value spectrum of the associator mass matrix over 3-frames on the Stiefel manifold $\\mathrm{St}(7,3)$ admits exactly one geometric ladder, the golden-ratio ladder $(1, \\varphi^{-1}, \\varphi^{-2})$, and cannot realize the Cabibbo hierarchy $(\\lambda \\approx 0.22)$ — a fact we reduce to a three-line theorem (alternativity forces a traceless nonnegative matrix, hence $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$, hence $1 = x + x^2$). We then asked whether this specific algebraic structure has value as an inductive bias in a neural network. We implemented the associator \"mass matrix\" as a parameter-starved PyTorch layer (31 trainable parameters) and evaluated it against an unconstrained baseline (46 parameters) across a 60-cell grid spanning three data-generating teachers, four label-noise levels, and five training-set sizes, followed by a 5-seed replication of the contested cells. The layer behaves exactly like a strict architectural prior in the sense familiar from convolutional networks: on associator-structured data it is weakly dominant — never significantly worse than the baseline, and up to $2\\times$ better in held-out error under data scarcity or label noise, reaching the irreducible noise floor $\\sigma^2$ — while on data generated outside its function class it is strictly dominated once training data is adequate, by up to $15.6\\times$. The advantage does not require the golden-ratio configuration: unregularized models generalize equally well at other points of the associator class. A capacity-matched mechanism experiment (600 runs) then localizes the source of the advantage: scrambled-tensor and Stiefel-slice controls at identical parameter count are statistically indistinguishable from both associator variants on associator-generated data (0–1 significant separations in 24 cells each), while all constrained models dominate the baseline in 23–24 of 24 cells. The operative prior is therefore the constrained fixed-mixing bottleneck, not the octonion algebra; the octonions are load-bearing for the spectral theorem and dispensable for the learning advantage. We state both boundaries quantitatively.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Introduction\n\n### 1.1 The physics origin\n\nDivision algebras have a long history as candidate organizing structures for the Standard Model fermion spectrum. The exceptional group $E_6$ admits a single-generation embedding in its fundamental $\\mathbf{27}$, which is naturally realized as the exceptional Jordan algebra $J_3(\\mathbb{O})$ of $3\\times 3$ Hermitian octonionic matrices. In such constructions the non-associativity of $\\mathbb{O}$ is not a nuisance but the load-bearing feature: the failure of the associative law is measured by the associator\n\n$$\n[x, y, z] \\;=\\; (x \\star y) \\star z \\;-\\; x \\star (y \\star z),\n$$\n\nand one may hope that mass ratios or mixing angles emerge from its spectral data. Concretely, we investigated whether a 3-frame of pure-imaginary octonions $\\{u_1, u_2, u_3\\}$, optimized against a fixed \"vacuum\" direction, could reproduce the observed fermion mass hierarchy, whose small parameter is the Cabibbo angle $\\lambda \\approx 0.2245$ (Wolfenstein parametrization: hierarchies of order $\\lambda^2, \\lambda^4, \\ldots$).\n\n### 1.2 The Golden Ratio anomaly\n\nThe attempt failed, and the failure was clean. A scan over orthonormal 3-frames $U \\in \\mathrm{St}(7,3)$ (the Stiefel manifold of 3-frames in the 7-dimensional imaginary octonion space) showed that the normalized singular-value spectrum of the associator-derived $3\\times3$ matrix *can* form a geometric ladder $(1, x, x^2)$ — but only at one base. Direct optimization reaches\n\n$$\n\\left(1,\\; \\varphi^{-1},\\; \\varphi^{-2}\\right) \\;=\\; (1,\\; 0.6180\\ldots,\\; 0.3819\\ldots), \\qquad \\varphi = \\tfrac{1+\\sqrt 5}{2},\n$$\n\nwith zero residual, while every other prescribed base — including the Cabibbo values $x = \\lambda^2$ and $x = \\lambda^4$ — is unreachable (residuals $\\mathcal{O}(10^{-1})$). Among $8000$ random frames, the 859 whose spectra were incidentally near-geometric all had base in $[0.614, 0.622]$, median $0.6181$. The golden ratio is not merely an attractor of this landscape; as we show in §2.4, it is the *unique* geometric ladder the operator admits, by an elementary theorem. The physical hierarchy is therefore not approximately disfavored but exactly impossible, and as a derivation of flavor physics the program is dead on arrival — provably.\n\n### 1.3 The pivot\n\nA stable, reproducible attractor in a constrained non-associative geometry is, however, precisely the raw material of an *inductive bias*. The machine-learning question is separable from the physics question: does constraining a network layer to the octonion associator's function class buy generalization when the data respects that class, and what does it cost when the data does not? The remainder of this paper answers that question empirically. We emphasize at the outset that the answer is bounded on both sides: the layer is neither useless nor a free lunch, and we map the boundary.\n\n## 2. The Non-Associative 3-Frame Operator\n\n### 2.1 Algebra\n\nLet $e_1, \\ldots, e_7$ denote the imaginary octonion units. The multiplication of pure-imaginary octonions $x = \\sum_i x_i e_i$, $y = \\sum_j y_j e_j$ has vector part\n\n$$\n(x \\star y)_k \\;=\\; \\sum_{i,j} x_i\\, y_j\\, C_{ijk},\n$$\n\nwhere $C_{ijk}$ are the totally antisymmetric structure constants determined by the Fano plane. With the index convention used throughout this project (0-indexed $e_1 \\to$ index 0), the seven oriented lines are the cyclic triples\n\n$$\n(1,2,4),\\;(2,3,5),\\;(3,4,6),\\;(4,5,7),\\;(5,6,1),\\;(6,7,2),\\;(7,1,3)\n$$\n\nin 1-indexed unit labels, each contributing $C_{ijk} = +1$ on its cyclic orderings and $-1$ on anticyclic ones. $C$ is stored as a fixed (non-trainable) $7\\times7\\times7$ buffer; all products are single `einsum` contractions,\n\n```python\nz = torch.einsum('...i,...j,ijk->...k', x, y, C)\n```\n\nBecause $\\mathbb{O}$ is non-associative, the associator of pure-imaginary elements against a fixed vacuum direction $V$ is generically nonzero. Define the **associator defect**\n\n$$\nD_{ab} \\;=\\; (u_a \\star u_b) \\star V \\;-\\; u_a \\star (u_b \\star V), \\qquad a, b \\in \\{1,2,3\\},\n$$\n\nand the **mass matrix**\n\n$$\nM_{ab} \\;=\\; \\left\\lVert D_{ab} \\right\\rVert^2 .\n$$\n\n$M$ is a $3\\times3$ matrix functional of the frame $\\{u_a\\}$ and vacuum $V$; it vanishes identically if the algebra is associative (e.g., if all arguments lie in a common quaternionic subalgebra), so any signal passing through $M$ is carried by non-associativity alone.\n\n### 2.2 The layer\n\nThe strict model used in all sweep experiments is deliberately parameter-starved:\n\n- A trainable raw frame $W \\in \\mathbb{R}^{7\\times3}$ (21 parameters), orthonormalized by QR decomposition to a Stiefel frame $U \\in \\mathrm{St}(7,3)$ on every forward pass.\n- A fixed, non-trainable vacuum $V = e_7$.\n- The mass matrix $M_{ab}(U, V)$, normalized by its largest element.\n- Input features $x \\in \\mathbb{R}^3$ enter through row scaling: the 9 features are $\\tanh(x_a M_{ab})$, flattened.\n- A linear readout $\\mathrm{Linear}(9 \\to 1)$ (10 parameters).\n\nTotal: **31 trainable parameters**. The baseline (\"free mixer\") is $\\mathrm{Linear}(3\\to9) \\to \\tanh \\to \\mathrm{Linear}(9\\to1)$: **46 trainable parameters**, strictly more expressive over the same feature width. The baseline can represent any $3\\times9$ mixing; the associator model can only realize mixings expressible as row-scaled octonion mass matrices. An earlier, less constrained variant of the layer (three unconstrained $3\\to7$ projections, a trainable vacuum, and singular values of $M$ appended to the feature vector via `torch.linalg.svdvals`; 104 parameters) was implemented first and retained for the Phase I experiments; all quantitative claims below about the 31-parameter model refer to the strict Stiefel version.\n\n### 2.3 A disclosure: the ML layer computes a truncated associator\n\nThe neural implementations in this paper compute octonion products by the single contraction $z_k = \\sum_{ij} x_i y_j C_{ijk}$, which returns only the *imaginary part* of the product. For pure-imaginary arguments the true product is $x \\star y = -\\langle x, y\\rangle + x \\times_\\phi y$: it also carries a scalar part, and that scalar re-enters nested products. Dropping it changes the operator. In particular, the truncated version is **not alternative**: the true associator satisfies $[u, u, V] = 0$ identically, whereas the truncated $D_{aa}$ is generically nonzero. The truncated mass matrix therefore has a nonvanishing diagonal and nine informative entries, where the true associator mass matrix is symmetric with an exactly zero diagonal — three degrees of freedom, not nine.\n\nAll ML results in this paper are internally consistent (teachers and students use the same truncated operator, so the function-class-match experiments measure what they claim), but the operator should be read as \"the vector-part truncation of the octonion associator,\" and we retain the shorter name only for brevity. The physics results of §1.2 and §2.4 use the exact algebra. A layer built on the exact associator would be even more parameter-starved (a 3-feature bottleneck) and is an obvious follow-up.\n\n### 2.4 Why the golden ratio: an exact result\n\nThe golden-ratio ladder of §1.2 admits a three-line proof, which to our knowledge went unnoticed during the original scan.\n\n**Theorem.** Let $M_{ab} = \\|[u_a, u_b, H]\\|^2$ for any orthonormal 3-frame $\\{u_a\\}$ and any fixed $H$ in the imaginary octonions. If the normalized singular-value spectrum of $M$ is a geometric ladder $(1, x, x^2)$ with $x > 0$, then $x = \\varphi^{-1}$.\n\n*Proof.* (i) The octonions are alternative, so the associator is totally antisymmetric in its arguments; in particular $[u_a, u_a, H] = 0$, so $M$ is symmetric with zero diagonal, hence traceless, and its entries are squared norms, hence nonnegative. (ii) For a symmetric nonnegative matrix, Perron–Frobenius gives $\\lambda_1 = \\rho(M) \\geq |\\lambda_2|, |\\lambda_3|$ with $\\lambda_1 \\geq 0$; tracelessness ($\\lambda_1 + \\lambda_2 + \\lambda_3 = 0$) then forces $\\lambda_2, \\lambda_3 \\leq 0$ (if $\\lambda_2 > 0$ then $|\\lambda_3| = \\lambda_1 + \\lambda_2 > \\lambda_1$, contradicting dominance), so the singular values $s_i = |\\lambda_i|$ satisfy $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$ identically. (iii) Imposing $(s_1, s_2, s_3) \\propto (1, x, x^2)$ yields $1 = x + x^2$, whose unique positive root is $x = \\tfrac{\\sqrt5 - 1}{2} = \\varphi^{-1}$. $\\square$\n\nWe verified step (ii) numerically: over 2000 random Stiefel frames, $|s_1 - (s_2 + s_3)|/s_1 \\leq 6.5\\times10^{-16}$.\n\nThree consequences. First, the golden ratio is a *theorem* of the operator, not an emergent or fine-tuned property: $1 = x + x^2$ is the defining equation of $\\varphi$, and alternativity plus nonnegativity smuggle it in. Second, the Cabibbo impossibility is equally exact — no geometric ladder with base $\\lambda^2$ exists for this operator at any frame. Third, the result is octonion-specific in a precise sense: it requires an algebra that is alternative (for the zero diagonal) but not associative (else $M \\equiv 0$), and the octonions are the unique normed division algebra in that intersection. We confirmed the negative direction empirically: replacing the Fano structure constants with random totally antisymmetric tensors, or with non-alternative truncations (including our own ML operator of §2.3), destroys the zero diagonal and with it the golden constraint — such operators reach self-similar ladders at a continuum of bases, none preferentially golden. A cautionary note from this project's own history: an earlier version of this test, run with the truncated operator of §2.3, wrongly suggested the golden ratio was an artifact; the discrepancy was traced to the truncation breaking alternativity. Structural claims about an algebra must be tested with the exact algebra.\n\n## 3. Benchmark Phase I: Linear Degeneracy\n\nThe first benchmark targeted the golden hierarchy directly. Inputs $X \\in \\mathbb{R}^{n\\times3}$ were rotated by a fixed random orthogonal matrix and labeled by\n\n$$\nY \\;=\\; X_{\\mathrm{rot}} \\cdot \\left(1,\\; \\varphi^{-1},\\; \\varphi^{-2}\\right)^{\\!\\top} + \\varepsilon .\n$$\n\nThree models were compared over 5 seeds: the free mixer (46 params), the associator model (31 params), and a regularized associator (34 params) whose singular-value ratios are penalized toward $(\\varphi^{-1}, \\varphi^{-1})$.\n\nThe result was an exact three-way tie. All three models reached test MSE $0.064720 \\pm 0.002162$, identical to six decimal places per seed. The regularized model did lock its internal ladder to $(1.000000,\\, 0.618034,\\, 0.381966)$ at no cost in MSE; the unregularized model drifted to ratios of roughly $0.56$–$0.60$ and predicted equally well.\n\nThe diagnosis is structural: the target is affine in the input, and every architecture above collapses to an effective affine map $\\mathbb{R}^3 \\to \\mathbb{R}$. The benchmark therefore measured only each model's ability to do noisy linear regression, which all possess. The downstream linear predictor absorbs the geometry, and nothing about the associator is load-bearing. Phase I is **inconclusive by design flaw**, and we flag it because negative controls of this shape are easy to mistake for evidence of parity.\n\n## 4. Benchmark Phase II: The 60-Cell Sweep\n\n### 4.1 Load-bearing teachers\n\nTo make the geometry load-bearing, labels must depend on the mass matrix nonlinearly and irreducibly. The teacher construction is:\n\n$$\nY \\;=\\; \\tanh\\!\\big(\\mathrm{flatten}(x_a M^*_{ab})\\big) \\cdot w \\;+\\; b \\;+\\; \\varepsilon, \\qquad \\varepsilon \\sim \\mathcal{N}(0, \\sigma^2),\n$$\n\nwith fixed readout $w \\in \\mathbb{R}^9$, $b$, and three choices of the hidden matrix $M^*$:\n\n1. **golden** — $M^*$ computed from the locked near-golden frame found by the physics optimization, with vacuum $e_7$;\n2. **random\\_associator** — $M^*$ from a random orthonormal frame and random unit vacuum: inside the layer's function class, but away from the golden attractor;\n3. **non\\_associator** — $M^*(x)$ produced per-sample by a frozen, randomly initialized MLP $(3 \\to 16 \\to \\mathrm{GELU} \\to 9)$, reshaped to $3\\times3$: outside the function class by construction.\n\nA preliminary run at a single grid point (teacher = golden analogue, $n_{\\mathrm{train}} = 48$, $\\sigma = 0.15$, 10 seeds) produced the motivating result: associator test MSE $0.0257 \\pm 0.0020$ and $0.0249 \\pm 0.0007$ across two 5-seed blocks, versus free-mixer $0.0491 \\pm 0.0082$ and $0.0614 \\pm 0.0043$ — the constrained model at the noise floor ($\\sigma^2 = 0.0225$) and the unconstrained model overfitting, with the ordering *reversed* on training MSE (free mixer $\\approx 0.005$–$0.008$, associator $\\approx 0.018$–$0.020$). That signature — the baseline memorizes better, the constrained model generalizes better — motivated the full sweep.\n\n### 4.2 Sweep design\n\nThe grid is the Cartesian product\n\n- teacher $\\in$ {golden, random\\_associator, non\\_associator},\n- $\\sigma \\in \\{0.0,\\, 0.05,\\, 0.15,\\, 0.30\\}$,\n- $n_{\\mathrm{train}} \\in \\{16,\\, 32,\\, 48,\\, 96,\\, 192\\}$,\n\nfor 60 cells; each cell trains both models (Adam, learning rate $10^{-2}$, 400 epochs, full batch) and evaluates on 2048 held-out samples at the same noise level. All computation is CPU-only with fixed seeds.\n\n### 4.3 Results\n\nFigure 1 shows the full sweep. The single-seed win map:\n\n```\ngolden:                 n_train:   16    32    48    96   192\n  sigma = 0.00                      A     F     F     F     F\n  sigma = 0.05                      A     A     A     F     F\n  sigma = 0.15                      A     A     A     A     F\n  sigma = 0.30                      A     A     A     A     A\n\nrandom_associator:                  A in all 20 cells\n\nnon_associator:                     F in 17/20 cells\n                                    (A only at sigma = 0.30, n <= 48)\n```\n\n![Figure 1: Test MSE versus training-set size for the three teachers. Solid: 31-parameter associator model. Dashed: 46-parameter free mixer. Colors: label-noise levels. Grey dashed line: noise floor sigma^2 = 0.0225 for sigma = 0.15.](paper_figure_1.png)\n\n**Key quantitative points.**\n\n- On **random\\_associator** data the associator model won **20/20** cells, with median MSE ratio (associator/free) $0.659$. Mean test MSE across the panel: $0.034$ versus $0.059$.\n- On **golden** data the associator won 13/20 cells (median ratio $0.762$; means $0.036$ vs $0.058$). In the $\\sigma = 0.15$ row the associator's test MSE sat at $0.023$–$0.027$ against the information-theoretic floor $\\sigma^2 = 0.0225$.\n- On **non\\_associator** data the free mixer won **17/20** cells (median ratio $1.690$; means $0.110$ vs $0.081$ in the associator's disfavor). The gap grows monotonically with data: at $\\sigma = 0$, $n_{\\mathrm{train}} = 192$, the free mixer reached test MSE $0.004124$ versus the associator's $0.064435$ — a factor of **15.6**. The associator's error plateaus at $\\approx 0.06$–$0.09$ regardless of sample size: an irreducible approximation-error floor from being confined to the wrong function class.\n\n### 4.4 Multi-seed replication of the boundary\n\nSingle-seed win maps overstate boundary sharpness. We re-ran all 20 golden cells and the non\\_associator $\\sigma = 0.30$ row with 5 seeds per cell (fresh data and fresh initialization per seed; models paired on identical data within a seed) and adopted the rule that a cell is a *win* only if the mean paired test-MSE gap exceeds one standard deviation of the gap; otherwise it is a *tie*.\n\nTwelve of 25 verdicts changed, every one of them a boundary cell:\n\n```\ngolden (5 seeds):       n_train:   16    32    48    96   192\n  sigma = 0.00                      A     A     tie   tie   tie\n  sigma = 0.05                      A     tie   tie   tie   tie\n  sigma = 0.15                      A     tie   A     A     tie\n  sigma = 0.30                      A     A     A     A     A\n\nnon_associator, sigma = 0.30:       tie   A     tie   F     F\n```\n\nEvery free-mixer \"win\" on the golden teacher was seed noise: under replication the free mixer does not significantly win a single golden cell, while one cell ($\\sigma = 0$, $n=32$) flipped to a significant associator win ($0.0010 \\pm 0.0011$ vs $0.0070 \\pm 0.0037$, 5/5 seeds). At high noise the associator's wins are decisive (e.g., $\\sigma = 0.30$, $n=32$: $0.108 \\pm 0.009$ vs $0.227 \\pm 0.068$, 5/5 seeds). Conversely, the free mixer's advantage on non-associator data with adequate samples is robust: at $n = 192$ it won 5/5 seeds, $0.121 \\pm 0.011$ vs $0.163 \\pm 0.009$. The associator's apparent small-$n$ wins on the mismatched teacher mostly dissolved into ties, consistent with generic shrinkage rather than geometry.\n\nThe replicated record on associator-class data is therefore: **11 wins, 9 ties, 0 losses**.\n\n### 4.5 The golden regularizer is not the source of the advantage\n\nAdding a penalty that locks the internal singular-value ladder to $(\\varphi^{-1}, \\varphi^{-1})$ succeeds at its stated goal — regularized models reach ratios $(1.000000,\\, 0.618034,\\, 0.381966)$ — but confers no measurable test-MSE benefit: regularized and unregularized associator models are statistically indistinguishable in every experiment ($0.0257$ vs $0.0257$ at the motivating grid point). Unregularized models generalize equally well while sitting at other points of the class, with ladders as far away as $(1,\\, 0.81,\\, 0.19)$. Two conclusions follow. First, the inductive power resides in the structure constants — the (truncated) associator function class itself — not in the golden eigenvalue configuration that the physics scan found. Second, the golden ladder is a property of the *exact* algebra's spectral geometry (the theorem of §2.4), not of the *prediction objective*; MSE alone never rediscovers it, and the truncated ML operator is not even subject to it.\n\n## 5. Interpretation: The CNN Analogy\n\nThe results reproduce, in miniature and with unusual sharpness, the profile of convolutional layers.\n\nA convolutional layer is a weight-sharing constraint that encodes translation equivariance. On natural images, where the generative process respects that symmetry, CNNs dominate fully-connected networks of far higher parameter count, most visibly in the small-data regime; on images with permuted pixels, where the symmetry is destroyed, the same constraint is an approximation-error floor that no amount of data removes. The octonion associator layer does the same with \"translation structure\" replaced by \"associator structure\":\n\n| | Convolution | Octonion associator |\n|---|---|---|\n| Encoded structure | translation equivariance | Fano-plane non-associativity |\n| In-class behavior | wins, especially small data | 11 wins / 9 ties / 0 losses; $\\le 2\\times$ lower test MSE; reaches $\\sigma^2$ |\n| Out-of-class behavior | floor on permuted pixels | plateau at $0.06$–$0.09$; up to $15.6\\times$ worse |\n| Failure mode | approximation error, not estimation error | same (plateau is flat in $n_{\\mathrm{train}}$) |\n\n### 5.1 Mechanism: the prior is the bottleneck, not the algebra\n\nThe CNN analogy raises the attribution question directly: convolution's advantage is provably about translation structure — is the associator layer's advantage about octonion structure? A dedicated mechanism experiment (600 runs; 5 models $\\times$ 4 teachers $\\times$ 6 cells $\\times$ 5 seeds) answers **no**. We compared, at identical 31-parameter capacity and identical architecture, (a) the truncated associator, (b) the exact associator (alternativity verified: zero-diagonal $M$, $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$ to $10^{-6}$), (c) a random non-alternative \"scrambled\" structure tensor, and (d) a linear Stiefel-slice control, against the 46-parameter free mixer, on teachers generated by both the truncated and the exact operators.\n\nUnder the one-standard-deviation paired rule, the exact associator separates from the scrambled tensor in 1 of 24 cells, from the truncated associator in 4 (losing all 4), and from the Stiefel slice in 5 — while beating the free mixer in 23 of 24. Pooled mean test MSE spans $0.0667$–$0.0676$ across the four constrained models versus $0.1262$ for the free mixer: the average within-quartet spread per cell ($0.0024$) is **24 times smaller** than the quartet's average lead over the baseline ($0.0590$). The exact algebra also buys nothing over the truncation, even on exact-operator teachers.\n\nThe correct description of the earlier sweep is therefore: the separating function class is *fixed, input-independent $3\\times3$ mixing bottlenecks* versus *input-dependent mixing* (the non-associator MLP teacher computes $M(x)$ per sample) — not octonionic versus non-octonionic. The result splits cleanly down the paper's two halves: the octonions are **load-bearing for the physics** (the theorem of §2.4 requires alternativity, and no scrambled tensor satisfies it) and **dispensable for the learning advantage** (any capacity-matched fixed-mixing bottleneck delivers it).\n\nTwo statements about what this result is **not**:\n\n1. **It is not a generic regularization trick.** If the advantage were mere shrinkage from having 31 rather than 46 parameters, it would persist on the non-associator teacher. It does not: with adequate data the free mixer wins there 5/5 seeds, and the associator's out-of-class error is flat in sample size — the signature of approximation error, not variance. The falsification condition built into the sweep behaved exactly as a falsification condition should.\n2. **It is not a claim of practical superiority.** All positive results are on synthetic data generated inside (or at) the layer's own function class. The honest reading is: *if* a data-generating process is associator-structured, a 31-parameter octonion layer extracts it at the noise floor where a 46-parameter free model overfits; *whether* natural processes with this structure exist is an open empirical question and the obvious next step.\n\n**Limitations.** Three caveats bound the claims. (i) The teachers are synthetic and the input dimension is small ($d=3$ inputs, $7$-dimensional algebra); nothing here demonstrates scaling. (ii) An early pilot suggested capacity-matched non-octonion controls might match the associator in-class; the mechanism experiment of §5.1 confirmed this at full seed count, and the paper's attribution has been revised accordingly — the octonion-specificity of the *learning* advantage is rejected, while the octonion-specificity of the *spectral theorem* stands. (iii) The win/tie/loss verdicts use a one-standard-deviation rule at 5 seeds, which is a coarse instrument; boundary cells labeled \"tie\" are ties at this resolution, not proofs of equality. (iv) As disclosed in §2.3, the ML operator is the vector-part truncation of the associator, not the exact associator; the benchmark conclusions are unaffected (teacher and student share the operator), but transfer of the §2.4 spectral rigidity to the ML layer should not be assumed, and an exact-associator layer (a 3-feature bottleneck) remains untested.\n\n## 6. Conclusion\n\nWe set out to derive the Cabibbo angle from octonionic geometry and instead derived the golden ratio, which is to say: the physics failed — and the failure is now understood exactly. Alternativity forces the associator mass matrix to be traceless and nonnegative, so its only geometric spectral ladder is the one solving $1 = x + x^2$; the golden ratio was never emergent, and the Cabibbo hierarchy was never available. The failure product — an operator with a provably rigid spectral geometry — survived translation into a machine-learning component with unusually well-characterized behavior. Across a 60-cell sweep and a 5-seed replication, the 31-parameter associator layer is weakly dominant against a 46-parameter unconstrained baseline whenever the data-generating process lies in its function class (never significantly worse; up to $2\\times$ better under scarcity and noise; at the noise floor $\\sigma^2$ where the baseline overfits), and strictly dominated outside that class once data is adequate (up to $15.6\\times$ worse, with a sample-size-independent error plateau). The golden-ratio configuration itself is dispensable; the Fano-plane function class is what carries the bias.\n\nThe mechanism experiment then completed the attribution: the learning advantage belongs to the capacity-constrained fixed-mixing bottleneck, which any structure tensor — octonionic, scrambled, or a bare Stiefel slice — delivers equally well; the octonion algebra is necessary for the golden-ratio theorem and unnecessary for the generalization win.\n\nThe result is deliberately modest and, we believe, exact: a strict architectural prior with the same epistemic status as convolution — valuable inside its function class, a liability outside it — whose boundary *and* whose mechanism have now been measured rather than asserted. The two halves of the project end symmetrically: the physics failed for a provable algebraic reason, and the machine-learning success succeeds for a reason that has nothing to do with the algebra.\n\n---\n\n## Reproducibility\n\nAll experiments are CPU-only, seeded, and deterministic. Code and data accompany this document:\n\n| Artifact | Contents |\n|---|---|\n| `layer.py` | Original (104-parameter) associator layer; Fano structure constants |\n| `benchmark_sweep.py` | Strict 31-parameter model, teacher factory, 60-cell sweep |\n| `benchmark_sweep_multiseed.py` | 5-seed boundary replication |\n| `sweep_results.csv` | Raw 60-cell results |\n| `multiseed_results.csv` | Raw 250-run replication results |\n| `RESULTS.md` | Full experimental log, including the two inconclusive/confounded early benchmarks and the retracted fingerprint test |\n| `fingerprint_test.py` / `fingerprint_results.csv` | The (retracted) truncated-operator ladder test of §2.4's cautionary note |\n| `mechanism_test.py` / `mechanism_results.csv` | The §5.1 mechanism experiment (exact vs truncated vs scrambled vs slice) |\n| `make_paper_figure.py` / `paper_figure_1.png` | Figure 1 |\n\nTraining in every experiment: Adam, $\\mathrm{lr} = 10^{-2}$, full-batch, 400 epochs (500–1000 in Phase I variants), MSE loss; test sets of 1024–2048 samples at matched noise.\n\n# Blind Ablation Benchmark Results: Non-Associative Octonion Layer\n\n## Experimental Setup\n\n**Task**: Linear hierarchy regression on 3-feature inputs  \n**True Model**: Y = X_rotated @ [1.0, 1/φ, (1/φ)²] + ε(σ=0.2)  \n**Dataset**: 2000 samples with random orthogonal feature rotation  \n**Training**: 300 epochs, Adam optimizer (lr=0.05)  \n**Device**: CPU (no CUDA)  \n\n## Blind Test Results\n\n| Model Name | Final MSE Loss | Trainable Parameters | Parameters/Loss Ratio |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **FreeMixerModel** (baseline) | **0.038591** | 46 | 1.19 |\n| AssociatorModel | 2.987475 | 104 | 0.035 |\n| AssociatorRegModel | 2.175762 | 260 | 0.119 |\n\n## Detailed Findings\n\n### FreeMixerModel (Baseline)\n- **Architecture**: Linear(3→9) → Linear(9→1)\n- **Final MSE**: 0.038591\n- **Parameter Efficiency**: Best-in-class\n- **Convergence**: Rapid and stable\n\n### AssociatorModel\n- **Architecture**: AssociatorLadderLayer(3→1) with octonion mass matrix\n- **Final MSE**: 2.987475 (77.4× worse than baseline)\n- **Performance Gap**: -2.949 MSE units\n- **Assessment**: Severe degradation; octonion constraints inhibit learning\n\n### AssociatorRegModel\n- **Architecture**: AssociatorLadderLayer(3→12) → Linear(12→1) with SV regularization\n- **Final MSE**: 2.175762 (56.4× worse than baseline)\n- **Performance Gap**: -2.137 MSE units\n- **Regularization Effect**: Modest improvement over AssociatorModel, but still catastrophic\n\n## Scientific Verdict\n\n**The non-associative octonion layer has zero machine learning utility on this task.**\n\nThe unconstrained linear baseline achieves **0.038591 MSE**, while the best Associator variant (with regularization) achieves **2.175762 MSE**—a performance degradation of over 56×.\n\n### Key Observations\n\n1. **Constraint Failure**: The non-associative geometric constraints embedded in the octonion algebra severely hamper the model's capacity to fit the data. The associativity-violation mass matrix appears to encode irrelevant geometric properties that have no correlation with the linear regression task.\n\n2. **Parameter Inefficiency**: Despite using 5.7× more parameters (260 vs 46), the regularized Associator model fails catastrophically. This suggests the octonion projection space does not align with the underlying data manifold.\n\n3. **Optimization Landscape**: The mass matrix computation (measuring ||（u_a * u_b) * v - u_a * (u_b * v)||²) creates an intermediate feature representation that is hostile to learning linear relationships. The 12-dimensional bottleneck does not preserve the task-relevant structure.\n\n4. **Regularization Minimal Impact**: Regularizing the singular value ratios toward the golden ratio (1/φ) provides only 27% improvement over the unregularized variant, suggesting the octonion geometry fundamentally conflicts with the linear hierarchy structure.\n\n## Conclusion\n\n**On linear regression tasks, unconstrained parameterization dominates geometrically-constrained non-associative algebras.**\n\nFor the task of learning a linear hierarchy (Y = X @ w + ε), the FreeMixerModel's superior performance (47× parameter efficiency vs Associator-Reg) definitively demonstrates that:\n\n- Non-associative octonion geometry introduces unnecessary inductive bias\n- The associativity-violation mass matrix does not capture task-relevant features\n- Parameter-efficient linear models are provably superior on this benchmark\n\n**Recommendation**: This layer shows no promise for standard regression/classification tasks. Future work should explore whether non-associative geometry could be valuable in domains with inherent non-associative structure (e.g., certain algebraic or physical systems), rather than generic ML tasks.\n\n---\n\n**Blind Test Status**: NEGATIVE  \n**Associator Layer Utility**: NOT DEMONSTRATED  \n**Winner**: Free Linear Mixer Baseline\n\n---\n\n# Experiment 2: Load-Bearing Non-Linear Trap (`benchmark_nonlinear_trap.py`)\n\n## Setup\n\n**Target**: Y = M12·M23 − 0.5·M13², where M is the TRUE octonion associator mass\nmatrix computed from fixed random 7D projections (seed 99) and a fixed vacuum\n(seed 100). Target standardized to unit variance, noise σ=0.05.\n**Data**: 3000 samples (2000 train / 1000 test). Training: 500 epochs, Adam lr=0.01, CPU.\n\n## Results\n\n| Model | Final Test MSE | Parameters |\n|---|---|---|\n| Baseline_MLP (3→64→64→1, GELU) | 0.29896942 | 4,481 |\n| Associator_Trap (AssociatorLadderLayer → Linear(9,1)) | 2.07922578 | 218 |\n\n**VERDICT: FAIL.** The constrained geometry lost to the generic MLP by ~7×\ndespite the data being generated by the exact octonion math the layer hardcodes.\n\n## Interpretation\n\n1. **Expressivity mismatch, not geometry failure.** The target is *quadratic* in\n   the mass-matrix elements, but Associator_Trap's readout is a single linear\n   layer over (a linear mixture of) those elements. A linear readout cannot\n   represent products of M-entries, so the model is structurally incapable of\n   fitting this target regardless of geometric alignment.\n2. **Layer output is not raw M.** Per the unmodified `layer.py`, the 9 output\n   features are `Linear(12→9)` over `[M_flat, SVs]` — a learned mixture, still\n   linear in M.\n3. **Both models struggled.** The MLP reached only R² ≈ 0.7 on test with severe\n   overfitting (train MSE 0.0026 vs test 0.299); the Associator was still\n   improving at epoch 500 (train 4.1 → 0.89) but generalizing poorly (test 2.08).\n\n## Conclusion\n\nHardcoded octonion geometry alone did not confer a parameter-efficiency\nadvantage here, because the benchmark conflated two requirements: matching the\ndata-generating *geometry* (which the layer has) and matching the *functional\nform* of the readout (quadratic in M, which the layer lacks). A follow-up with a\nquadratic readout over the 9 associator features (~45 extra parameters) would\nisolate the geometric contribution cleanly.\n\n**Trap Test Status**: NEGATIVE (with identified expressivity confound)  \n**Winner**: Baseline MLP\n\n---\n\n# Experiment 3: 3D Boundary Sweep (`benchmark_sweep.py`)\n\n## Setup\n\nGrid: 3 teachers x 4 noise levels (0.0/0.05/0.15/0.30) x 5 training sizes\n(16/32/48/96/192) = 60 cells. Models: strict 31-param Associator (21 Stiefel\nframe params + Linear(9,1)) vs 46-param FreeMixer (tanh MLP). 400 epochs,\nAdam lr=0.01, 2048 test samples per cell. Artifacts: `sweep_results.csv`,\n`sweep_plots.png`.\n\n## Win Map (A = Associator wins on test MSE, F = FreeMixer wins)\n\n```\ngolden:              n_train:  16   32   48   96   192\n  noise=0.00                    A    F    F    F    F\n  noise=0.05                    A    A    A    F    F\n  noise=0.15                    A    A    A    A    F\n  noise=0.30                    A    A    A    A    A\n\nrandom_associator:  Associator wins ALL 20 cells.\n\nnon_associator:     FreeMixer wins 17/20; Associator wins only the three\n                    smallest-data, highest-noise cells (noise=0.3, n<=48).\n```\n\nMedian Assoc/Free test-MSE ratio (<1 favors Associator):\ngolden 0.762 | random_associator 0.659 | non_associator 1.690.\n\n## Interpretation\n\n1. **The advantage is teacher-class recovery, not generic regularization.**\n   The Associator dominates exactly when the data-generating process is\n   associator-structured (all 20 random_associator cells, 13/20 golden cells)\n   and loses decisively when it is not (17/20 non_associator cells, with the\n   gap growing to 15.6x at noise=0, n_train=192).\n2. **The falsification condition behaved correctly.** On the non-associator\n   teacher the FreeMixer improves steadily with data while the Associator\n   plateaus around test MSE ~0.06-0.09 — an irreducible approximation-error\n   floor from being constrained to the wrong function class.\n3. **The advantage boundary follows the noise/data ratio.** On the golden\n   teacher the FreeMixer overtakes when data is plentiful relative to noise\n   (n_train >= 96 at sigma=0.05, n_train=192 at sigma=0.15, everywhere at\n   sigma=0); at sigma=0.30 the Associator wins at every training size. The\n   frontier is roughly where the FreeMixer has enough clean samples to\n   estimate its 46 parameters.\n4. **Winning cells hug the noise floor.** Associator test MSE at sigma=0.15\n   sits at ~0.023-0.027 against the sigma^2 = 0.0225 floor.\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe octonion associator constraint is a genuine, specific inductive bias:\nit buys roughly 1.3-2x lower held-out error in the small-data / high-noise\nregime when the target is truly associator-generated, and it costs up to an\norder of magnitude when the target is not. This is the textbook signature of\na correct (but narrow) architectural prior, analogous to convolutional\nweight-sharing: valuable inside its function class, a liability outside it.\n\n**Sweep Status**: BOUNDARY MAPPED (single seed — superseded by Experiment 4)  \n**Associator advantage**: real, confined to associator-class teachers under\ndata scarcity or label noise; FreeMixer wins with abundant clean data or a\nmismatched teacher.\n\n---\n\n# Experiment 4: Multi-Seed Boundary Replication (`benchmark_sweep_multiseed.py`)\n\n## Setup\n\n5 seeds per cell (fresh data AND fresh init per seed, models paired on\nidentical data within each seed). Cells: all 20 golden-teacher cells plus the\nnon_associator noise=0.30 row. Decision rule: a model wins a cell only if\n|mean paired test-MSE gap| > 1 std of the paired gap; otherwise TIE.\nRaw data: `multiseed_results.csv` (250 rows).\n\n## Verdict Map (5 seeds, 1-std rule)\n\n```\ngolden:              n_train:   16     32     48     96     192\n  noise=0.00                    A      A      TIE    TIE    TIE\n  noise=0.05                    A      TIE    TIE    TIE    TIE\n  noise=0.15                    A      TIE    A      A      TIE\n  noise=0.30                    A      A      A      A      A\n\nnon_associator:\n  noise=0.30                    TIE    A      TIE    F      F\n```\n\n12 of 25 single-seed verdicts changed under reseeding — every change was a\nboundary cell collapsing to TIE (plus one flip to Associator at golden\nsigma=0, n=32).\n\n## Key revisions to the single-seed story\n\n1. **The FreeMixer's golden-teacher \"wins\" were seed noise — all of them.**\n   With error bars, the FreeMixer does not significantly win a single golden\n   cell. The multi-seed record on golden: Associator 11 wins, 9 ties,\n   0 losses. At sigma=0 with abundant data, both models sit at ~0.001-0.002\n   MSE and are statistically indistinguishable.\n2. **The Associator's advantage region is confirmed and clean.** All 5/5\n   seeds favor it in every high-noise cell; at sigma=0.30 it wins at every\n   training size with gaps of 3-13x the gap std.\n3. **The non_associator falsification still holds where it matters.** With\n   ample data (n>=96) the FreeMixer wins 5/5 seeds decisively. The\n   small-data, high-noise Associator \"wins\" there are mostly ties (only\n   n=32 survives the 1-std rule) — consistent with generic shrinkage, not\n   geometry, helping when the free model overfits 0.3-noise labels.\n\n## Revised conclusion\n\nOn associator-class data the strict 31-param Associator **never loses** to the\n46-param FreeMixer at any tested (noise, n_train); it significantly wins\nwhenever data is scarce or noise is substantial, and ties otherwise. Against\nnon-associator data with adequate samples it loses decisively. The defensible\none-line claim:\n\n> Within its function class the octonion associator prior is weakly dominant\n> (win or tie everywhere, wins concentrated in the scarce-data/high-noise\n> regime); outside its class it is strictly dominated once data is adequate.\n\n**Multi-seed Status**: BOUNDARY CONFIRMED AND SHARPENED  \n**Winner inside the associator class**: Associator (never significantly worse)  \n**Winner outside the class with n>=96**: FreeMixer\n\n---\n\n# Experiment 5: Golden-Ratio Fingerprint Test and Its Resolution\n# (`fingerprint_test.py` + original repo `D:\\Projects\\FINALFUCKINGTIME`)\n\n## Part A: the fingerprint test (2026-07-09, RETRACTED as a test of the claim)\n\nQuestion: is the golden-ratio ladder an intrinsic attractor of octonion\ngeometry, or an artifact of the original scan's objective?\n\nMethod: optimize Stiefel 3-frames toward self-similar spectral ladders\n(objective `(s2/s1 - s3/s2)^2`, phi-free) for 7 structure-constant families\n(genuine Fano, 3 shuffled-triple imposters, 3 random antisymmetric tensors),\n12 starts each. Result: all 84 runs converged; ZERO landed at phi^-1. Fano\nratios clustered at 0.32-0.43 (median 0.393); imposters scattered 0.09-0.49.\nPreliminary verdict at the time: golden ratio not supported.\n\n**That verdict was wrong, for an instructive reason (Part C).**\n\n## Part B: the original evidence (from `fn_ladder_scan.py` / results JSON)\n\nThe original scan's own data, re-read:\n- Random scan (8000 frames): the 859 frames with incidentally near-geometric\n  spectra ALL had base in [0.6136, 0.6225], median 0.61810.\n- Free-ratio geometric optimization: converged to (1, 0.618034, 0.381966)\n  with objective exactly 0.\n- Prescribed-base optimizations: base phi^-1 reached residual 0; every other\n  base (incl. Cabibbo lambda^2 = 0.0503) unreachable, residuals O(0.1).\n- All achieved spectra satisfy r1 + r2 = 1.\n\n## Part C: resolution — the golden ratio is a THEOREM\n\nFor the TRUE octonion associator, M_ab = ||[u_a, u_b, e7]||^2 satisfies:\n1. Alternativity => [u,u,H] = 0 => M symmetric with exactly zero diagonal\n   (traceless), entries nonnegative.\n2. Perron-Frobenius (symmetric nonnegative) + tracelessness => lambda_2,\n   lambda_3 <= 0 and s1 = s2 + s3 identically. Verified numerically:\n   max relative deviation 6.5e-16 over 2000 random frames.\n3. Geometric ladder (1, x, x^2) + (s1 = s2+s3) => 1 = x + x^2 => x = phi^-1\n   (the defining equation of the golden ratio). Unique. Cabibbo impossible.\n\nWhy Part A missed it: `layer.py`'s `_oct_mul` keeps only the VECTOR PART of\noctonion products, dropping scalar parts. The truncation breaks alternativity\n([u,u,V] != 0), giving M a nonzero diagonal, destroying the trace-zero\nconstraint and with it the golden equation. The fingerprint test tested a\ndifferent (non-alternative) algebra. Its one durable finding: the truncated\nFano operator still has a distinctive ratio band (~0.39) vs imposters.\n\n## Consequences\n\n1. Golden ratio: PROVEN, not emergent. Cabibbo impossibility: exact theorem.\n2. Octonion-specificity is precise: requires alternative-but-not-associative,\n   i.e. the octonions among normed division algebras.\n3. The ML layer (and the sweep's teachers/models) use the truncated operator:\n   internally consistent benchmarks, but not the exact associator. An\n   exact-associator layer would have a 3-feature bottleneck (symmetric,\n   zero-diagonal M) — untested, queued as future work.\n4. Methodological lesson: structural claims about an algebra must be tested\n   with the exact algebra; a null result from a mis-specified operator reads\n   identically to a true null.\n\n**Status**: GOLDEN RATIO VINDICATED (theorem); fingerprint test retracted\nwith diagnosis; PAPER.md updated (new sections 2.3, 2.4).\n\n---\n\n# Experiment 6: Mechanism Test (`mechanism_test.py`)\n\n## Setup\n\n600 training runs: 5 models x 4 teachers x {noise 0.15, 0.30} x\n{n_train 16, 48, 192} x 5 seeds. Models (params): FreeMixer (46),\nTruncAssociator (31, vector-part tensor), ExactAssociator (31, exact\nassociator tensor, alternativity verified: zero-diagonal M, s1=s2+s3),\nScrambledTensor (31, random non-alternative tensor, same architecture),\nStiefelSlice (31, linear frame slice). Teachers: golden/random x\ntruncated/exact operators. Raw data: mechanism_results.csv.\n\n## Results (1-std paired-gap rule, 24 cells per comparison)\n\n- ExactAssociator vs TruncAssociator: 0 wins / 20 ties / 4 losses.\n- ExactAssociator vs ScrambledTensor: 0 wins / 23 ties / 1 loss.\n- ExactAssociator vs StiefelSlice:    1 win  / 19 ties / 4 losses.\n- ExactAssociator vs FreeMixer:      23 wins /  1 tie  / 0 losses.\n\nPooled mean test MSE: ScrambledTensor 0.0667, ExactAssociator 0.0672,\nTruncAssociator 0.0673, StiefelSlice 0.0676, FreeMixer 0.1262. Average\nwithin-quartet spread per cell 0.0024; average quartet lead over FreeMixer\n0.0590 (ratio 24.3x).\n\n## Conclusion\n\n**The in-class ML advantage is carried by the constrained-bottleneck\narchitecture (fixed input-independent 3x3 mixing matrix + tanh + small\nreadout), NOT by the octonion algebra.** A random non-alternative tensor and\neven a linear Stiefel slice are statistically indistinguishable from both\nassociator variants, on associator-generated data, at matched capacity.\nThe pilot's warning (Experiment 4 limitations) is confirmed at full power.\n\nReconciliation with the earlier sweep: the \"function class\" that separates\nwinners from losers is fixed-matrix bottlenecks vs input-dependent mixing\n(the non_associator MLP teacher computes M(x) per sample) — not octonionic\nvs non-octonionic. The octonions remain load-bearing for the PHYSICS result\n(the phi theorem requires alternativity) and irrelevant for the ML result.\n\n**Status**: MECHANISM RESOLVED — octonion-specificity of the ML advantage is\nREJECTED; capacity-constrained bottleneck prior confirmed. The physics\ntheorem (Experiment 5) is unaffected.\n\n---\n\n# Experiment 7: The k-bonacci Family (`tribonacci_test.py` + n=5..7 sweep)\n\n## Question\n\nTHEOREM_NOTE open question: for n-frames (n >= 4), does the sum rule\ns1 = sum(s_i, i>=2) survive (matrix theory no longer forces it, per\nCharles-Farber-Johnson-Kennedy-Shaffer 2013), and are geometric ladders\nrealized at the reciprocal k-bonacci bases solving 1 = x + ... + x^(n-1)?\n\n## Results (exact associator tensor B_EXACT, float64)\n\n1. **Sum rule: universal.** Max relative deviation ~1e-15 over 5000-20000\n   random frames per size, n = 4..7; 0/20000 frames with a positive\n   subdominant eigenvalue at n=4. Not implied by matrix theory — stated as\n   the Universal Sum Rule Conjecture (proof likely via G2 invariance).\n2. **Ladders realized exactly for n = 4, 5, 6** (k-bonacci-free objective):\n   - n=4: 24/24 starts -> (1, .54369, .29560, .16071), tribonacci to 7 digits.\n   - n=5: tetranacci 0.5187901, residual 3e-32.\n   - n=6: pentanacci 0.5086604, residual 1e-30.\n3. **n=7: near-miss.** 28 starts, two barrier configs: residual stalls at\n   ~1.5e-8 (vs machine zero for n<=6), base 0.5049-0.5054 vs hexanacci\n   0.5041383, deviation concentrated in the two smallest rungs; sum rule\n   still 1e-16. Read as evidence the exact ladder is NOT realizable at n=7\n   (moduli collapse to O(7)/G2); proof open.\n   Methodological note: the first n=7 run failed for a different reason —\n   the anti-degeneracy barrier (0.02) EXCLUDED the target (hexanacci's\n   smallest rung x^6 = 0.0163 < 0.02). Barrier moved to 0.005 before the\n   verdict above. Check your guard rails against the hypothesis.\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe golden-ratio theorem is the n=3 member of a k-bonacci family: the\noctonion associator realizes precisely the geometric ladders whose base\nsatisfies 1 = x + ... + x^(n-1), for every frame size tested except the\ndegenerate full-basis case n=7, which it near-misses. Written up in\nTHEOREM_NOTE.tex (section 3, Proposition + Conjecture + Remark).\n\n**Status**: OPEN QUESTION ANSWERED (n=4,5,6 exact; n=7 near-miss, open);\nnote upgraded to arXiv-ready LaTeX with prior-art citations.\n\n## Addendum: n=7 Jacobian test (`jacobian_test_n7.py`, referee request)\n\nAt 3 independently converged stall points: gradient ||J^T c|| ~ 1e-8 (true\ncritical points); Jacobian of the 5 ladder constraints effectively rank 4\n(sigma_5/sigma_1 ~ 1e-3 vs 4 healthy values); residual c aligned with the\ncollapsed direction to |cos| = 1.0000; identical c-signature across seeds\n(one canonical critical manifold). VERDICT: hexanacci exclusion upgraded from\n\"0/28 runs\" to \"first-order obstruction\" — 4 of 5 conditions satisfiable, the\n5th blocked to first order. Analytic follow-up defined: identify the critical\nmanifold, show the 5th constraint's differential vanishes along it.\n\nReferee-driven polish also applied (2026-07-09): explicit structure-constant\nform M_ab = H^m H^m' Q^(ab)_mm' with K = 4 Phi.Phi (G2-covariance manifest;\nK precomputed in octonion.py::build_K_tensor); honest epistemic labels\n(theorem / numerically exact / numerically excluded) on all scoreboards;\nuniqueness caveat (golden = unique GEOMETRIC spectrum; full sum-rule segment\nr in [0.5006, 0.9994] realizable) in paper, note, and one-pager.\n\n# SPEC SHEET — Octonion Associator Spectral System\n\nEngineering specification for the algebra, the spectral operator, the ML\nmodels, and their verified properties. Unified notation per `EQUATIONS.md`\n(Part II). Date: 2026-07-09.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Algebra layer\n\n| Item | Specification |\n|---|---|\n| Algebra | Octonions $\\mathbb{O}$; imaginary subspace $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O}) \\cong \\mathbb{R}^7$, units $e_1 \\ldots e_7$ |\n| Canonical convention | `FINALFUCKINGTIME/octonion.py`: oriented Fano triples $(1,2,3), (1,4,5), (6,1,7), (2,4,6), (2,5,7), (3,4,7), (5,3,6)$ |\n| Secondary convention | `layer.py` (0-indexed cycle $(0,1,3)$ mod 7). **Not interoperable** with canonical — never mix tensors across conventions |\n| Core tensors | $\\phi_{ijk}$ (3-form, 42 nonzero entries $\\pm1$); $\\Phi = \\tfrac16 \\varepsilon \\phi$ (Hodge dual); $A = -2\\Phi$ (associator tensor, verified on import) |\n| Slot tensor $\\mathsf{B}$ | $\\mathsf{B}_{ijk} = A_{ij7k}$; shape $(7,7,7)$; 24 nonzero entries $= \\pm2$; $\\|\\mathsf{B}\\|_F = \\sqrt{96} \\approx 9.798$; antisymmetric in $(i,j)$ |\n| Key property | Alternativity: $[x,x,z] = 0$. **Fragile** — destroyed by vector-part truncation (see §7) |\n| Self-checks | `octonion.py::verify_algebra()` (7 assoc + 28 non-assoc triples, $A = -2\\Phi$, antisymmetry); `mechanism_test.py::verify_exact_tensor()` (hollow + sum rule on 50 frames) — both run on import |\n\n## 2. Spectral operator\n\n| Item | Specification |\n|---|---|\n| Definition | $G[\\mathsf{T}](U)_{ab} = \\sum_k \\big( \\sum_{ij} U_{ia} U_{jb} \\mathsf{T}_{ijk} \\big)^2$ — one einsum + square + sum |\n| Domain | $U \\in \\mathrm{St}(7,n)$, $2 \\leq n \\leq 7$ (via QR of unconstrained $7 \\times n$); results hold for arbitrary non-orthonormal frames and arbitrary vacuum $H$ |\n| Output | $n \\times n$ symmetric, entrywise nonnegative; **hollow** iff $\\mathsf{T}$ is $(i \\leftrightarrow j)$-antisymmetric |\n| Invariant (proved, $n=3$) | Sum rule $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$ (exact; Perron–Frobenius + tracelessness) |\n| Invariant (conjectured, $n \\leq 7$) | $s_1 = \\sum_{i \\geq 2} s_i$; verified $\\leq 1.2 \\times 10^{-15}$ over 45,000+ frames; 0 violations |\n| Spectral rigidity | Geometric spectra exist only at $x = 1/T_{n-1}$ (k-bonacci reciprocal): 0.6180340 / 0.5436890 / 0.5187901 / 0.5086604 / 0.5041383 for $n = 3..7$ |\n| Realization status | $n=3$: theorem. $n = 4,5,6$: machine-zero residuals ($10^{-28}$–$10^{-32}$), 40/40 converged starts. $n=7$: NOT realized — 28/28 starts stall at residual $1.5 \\times 10^{-8}$, base $0.5049$ (open problem) |\n| Excluded outputs | Any geometric spectrum at $x \\neq 1/T_{n-1}$; all strongly hierarchical textures $(1, \\epsilon, \\epsilon')$, $\\epsilon + \\epsilon' < 1$; FN/Cabibbo textures identically |\n\n## 3. Model catalogue (ML study)\n\n| Model | Construction | Params | Verdict (5-seed, 1-std rule) |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| FreeMixer | $W_2 \\tanh(W_1 x + b_1) + b_2$, $3{\\to}9{\\to}1$ | 46 | Loses in-class 23/24 cells; wins out-of-class ($M(x)$ teachers) with $n_{\\mathrm{train}} \\geq 96$ |\n| TruncAssociator | readout of $G[\\tilde{\\mathsf{B}}]$, Stiefel frame | 31 | In-class: 11W/9T/0L vs FreeMixer |\n| ExactAssociator | readout of $G[\\mathsf{B}]$ | 31 | Ties TruncAssociator (0W/20T/4L) — exactness buys nothing |\n| ScrambledTensor | readout of $G[\\mathsf{R}]$, random antisym tensor | 31 | Ties ExactAssociator 23/24 — algebra not load-bearing |\n| StiefelSlice | linear $3{\\times}3$ frame slice, same readout | 31 | Ties the quartet |\n| layer.py original | $\\tilde M$ + SVD features, $\\mathrm{Linear}(12,\\cdot)$ | 104 | Legacy; excluded from headline results |\n\nShared readout: $\\hat y = w^\\top \\tanh(\\mathrm{flat}(x_a \\hat G_{ab})) + b$, $\\hat G$ max-normalized.\n**Mechanism verdict:** capacity/bottleneck effect is 24× larger than any between-tensor difference. The operative prior is *fixed input-independent mixing*, not octonion structure.\n\n## 4. Teacher catalogue\n\n| Teacher | $M^*$ source | Class |\n|---|---|---|\n| golden / golden_exact | locked near-golden frame, truncated / exact tensor | fixed-matrix (in-class) |\n| random_associator / random_exact | random frame + vacuum, truncated / exact | fixed-matrix (in-class) |\n| non_associator | frozen MLP $3{\\to}16{\\to}9$, $M^*(x)$ per sample | input-dependent (out-of-class) |\n| linear (Exp 1) | $y = X_{\\mathrm{rot}} (1, \\varphi^{-1}, \\varphi^{-2})^\\top + \\varepsilon$ | degenerate (all models tie) |\n\nSignal head (all): $y = w^{*\\top} \\tanh(\\mathrm{flat}(x_a M^*_{ab})) + b^* + \\varepsilon$, $\\varepsilon \\sim \\mathcal{N}(0, \\sigma^2)$.\n\n## 5. Training & search specification\n\n| Item | Value |\n|---|---|\n| Optimizer | Adam; lr 0.01 (ML), 0.02–0.03 (spectral search, cosine anneal for $n=7$) |\n| Epochs / steps | 400 (ML benchmarks); 1,500–15,000 (spectral) |\n| Precision | float32 (ML), float64 (spectral / theorem verification) |\n| Ladder objective | $\\sum_i ((s_{i+1}^2 - s_i s_{i+2})/s_1^2)^2 + \\mathrm{relu}(c - s_n/s_1)$ |\n| **Barrier rule** | $c$ MUST be $< (1/T_{n-1})^{n-1}$ (target's smallest rung). $c = 0.02$ silently excluded hexanacci ($x^6 = 0.0163$) — cost one false verdict |\n| Seeds | Fixed integer seeds throughout; per-cell paired data between models; 5 seeds/cell for verdicts |\n| Verdict rule | Win iff $|\\text{mean paired gap}| > 1$ std of gap; else tie |\n| Hardware | CPU only (4GB VRAM insufficient); minutes per experiment |\n| Console | ASCII only (Windows cp1252) — Greek letters crash prints |\n\n## 6. Verified performance envelope (ML)\n\n| Regime | Result |\n|---|---|\n| In-class (fixed-matrix teacher), scarce/noisy data | 31-param bottleneck models reach noise floor $\\sigma^2$; up to 2× lower test MSE than FreeMixer; never significantly worse at any tested cell |\n| In-class, abundant clean data | Statistical tie with FreeMixer |\n| Out-of-class ($M(x)$ teacher), $n_{\\mathrm{train}} \\geq 96$ | FreeMixer wins 5/5 seeds; bottleneck models plateau at irreducible approximation error (~0.06–0.09) |\n| Attribution | Advantage transfers to ANY capacity-matched fixed-mixing model (scrambled tensor, linear slice) — do not market as octonionic |\n\n## 7. Failure modes & gotchas (all encountered, all documented)\n\n1. **Vector-part truncation** breaks alternativity → non-hollow $G$ → all spectral\n   theorems void. `layer.py` and everything built on its tensor is truncated.\n   Exact tensor lives only in `mechanism_test.py::build_exact_assoc_tensor()`.\n2. **Convention mixing**: two Fano conventions in the codebase (§1). Tensors are\n   not interchangeable.\n3. **Barrier-excludes-target** (§5): check guard rails against the hypothesis.\n4. **Single-seed verdicts lie**: 12/25 sweep cells flipped under 5-seed\n   replication. Never report a boundary from one seed.\n5. **cp1252 console**: `sys.stdout.reconfigure(encoding=\"utf-8\")` (as in\n   `octonion.py`) or ASCII-only prints.\n\n## 8. Open problems (spec for future work)\n\n| ID | Statement | Suggested attack |\n|---|---|---|\n| OP-1 | Universal sum rule: octonionic $G[\\mathsf{B}]$ image lies in the extreme hollow stratum for all $n \\leq 7$ | $G_2$-invariants of $\\phi$, $*\\phi$ (Harvey–Lawson calibrations) |\n| OP-2 | Hexanacci non-realizability at $n=7$ (moduli $O(7)/G_2$, dim 7 vs 5 constraints — count says fits, algebra says no) | exact critical-point analysis on $O(7)/G_2$ |\n| OP-3 | Does $G[\\mathsf{R}]$ (scrambled, hollow) *attain* its allowed k-bonacci ladders? Decides whether attainment (not just rigidity) is octonion-specific | rerun `tribonacci_test.py` with $\\mathsf{R}$ — one afternoon |\n\n## 9. File map\n\n| Layer | Files |\n|---|---|\n| Exact algebra | `FINALFUCKINGTIME/octonion.py` (canonical); `mechanism_test.py` (torch port + checks) |\n| Spectral experiments | `fn_ladder_scan.py` (+results), `fingerprint_test.py` (retracted), `tribonacci_test.py` |\n| ML benchmarks | `benchmark.py`, `benchmark_nonlinear_trap.py`, `benchmark_sweep.py`, `benchmark_sweep_multiseed.py`, `mechanism_test.py` |\n| Data | `sweep_results.csv`, `multiseed_results.csv`, `mechanism_results.csv`, `fingerprint_results.csv` |\n| Write-ups | `SPECTRAL_LADDERS_PAPER.md`, `THEOREM_NOTE.tex/.md`, `PAPER.md`, `ONE_PAGER.md`, `quad_sheet.html`, `EQUATIONS.md` (this doc's companion), `RESULTS.md` (log), `HANDOFF.md` (closeout) |\n| Figures | `paper_figure_1.png`, `ladder_figure.png`, `sweep_plots.png` |\n\n# The k-Bonacci Spectral Ladders of the Octonion Associator\n\n**Abstract.** We describe a rigidity phenomenon in the spectral geometry of the octonion associator. For a frame of $n$ imaginary octonions $u_1, \\ldots, u_n$ and a vacuum direction $H$, the associator Gram matrix $M_{ab} = \\|[u_a, u_b, H]\\|^2$ is hollow (zero-diagonal), symmetric, and entrywise nonnegative — the first property a direct consequence of alternativity. For $n = 3$ this forces the exact singular-value sum rule $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$, so the only geometric ladder $(1, x, x^2)$ the operator can realize satisfies $1 = x + x^2$: the base is the inverse golden ratio, as a theorem. Numerically the pattern extends to a full family: the sum rule $s_1 = \\sum_{i \\geq 2} s_i$ holds at relative precision $10^{-15}$ on every sampled frame for all $n \\leq 7$ — although matrix theory ceases to enforce it at $n = 4$ — and unbiased gradient searches realize essentially all of that family exactly (to machine precision for $n \\leq 6$), at the reciprocal k-bonacci constants: golden ($n=3$), tribonacci ($n=4$), tetranacci ($n=5$), pentanacci ($n=6$). The terminal case $n = 7$, where the frame exhausts $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$, is a reproducible near-miss: searches stall at residual $\\sim 10^{-8}$ with base $0.5049$ against the hexanacci value $0.50414$. We state the universal sum rule as a conjecture (plausibly provable via $G_2$-invariance), record the $n=7$ non-realizability as an open problem, and note the phenomenological corollary: Froggatt–Nielsen-type mass hierarchies are strictly excluded from this operator class at every frame size.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Introduction\n\nThe octonions $\\mathbb{O}$ are the largest normed division algebra, and the unique one that is *alternative but not associative*: the associator\n\n$$\n[x, y, z] = (xy)z - x(yz)\n$$\n\nis nonzero in general, yet totally antisymmetric in its arguments (Artin's theorem), vanishing whenever two arguments coincide. This paper concerns a spectral consequence of that antisymmetry which, to our knowledge, has not been recorded: the associator's natural Gram matrices can only form *self-similar (geometric) spectra* at a specific countable family of bases — the reciprocals of the k-bonacci constants — and they realize essentially all of that family.\n\nThe object of study is the map sending an $n$-tuple (\"frame\") $u_1, \\ldots, u_n \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ and a fixed vacuum $H \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ to\n\n$$\nM_{ab}(U; H) \\;=\\; \\big\\| [u_a, u_b, H] \\big\\\\|^2, \\qquad a, b \\in \\{1, \\ldots, n\\}, \\quad n \\leq 7 .\n$$\n\nThis operator arose in an attempt to derive Standard Model fermion mass hierarchies from octonionic geometry, where the desired output was a Froggatt–Nielsen texture — a spectrum $(1, x, x^2)$ with Cabibbo-suppressed base $x = \\lambda^2 \\approx 0.05$. That program failed in an unusually instructive way: numerical scans found the operator *could* produce geometric spectra, but only at base $0.618\\ldots$, and optimization toward any other base stalled at large residuals. The failure is explained by the theorem below; the generalization to larger frames (§4) is new.\n\n## 2. Structure: the associator Gram matrix is hollow\n\n**Lemma 1.** *For arbitrary $u_1, \\ldots, u_n, H \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ — no orthonormality, no genericity — $M(U;H)$ is symmetric, entrywise nonnegative, and hollow ($M_{aa} \\equiv 0$), hence traceless.*\n\n*Proof.* Entries are squared norms (nonnegative). Alternativity makes the associator antisymmetric in its first two slots, so $[u_b, u_a, H] = -[u_a, u_b, H]$ (equal norms: symmetry) and $[u_a, u_a, H] = 0$ (hollowness). $\\square$\n\n### 2.1 Explicit form and manifest $G_2$-covariance\n\nFor any algebraic argument the one-line definition should be expanded. With $\\phi_{ijk}$ the Fano 3-form, $\\Phi = \\tfrac16 \\varepsilon \\phi$ its Hodge dual, and $A_{ijml} = [e_i, e_j, e_m]_l = -2\\,\\Phi_{ijml}$ the associator tensor, trilinearity gives\n\n$$\n[u_a, u_b, H]_l \\;=\\; \\sum_{i,j,m} u_a^{\\,i}\\, u_b^{\\,j}\\, H^{m}\\, A_{ijml},\n$$\n\nso the Gram matrix is an explicit quadratic form **in the vacuum**:\n\n$$\nM_{ab} \\;=\\; \\sum_{m,m'} H^{m} H^{m'}\\, Q^{(ab)}_{mm'}, \\qquad\nQ^{(ab)}_{mm'} \\;=\\; \\sum_{i,j,i',j'} u_a^{\\,i} u_b^{\\,j} u_a^{\\,i'} u_b^{\\,j'}\\, K_{iji'j'mm'}, \\qquad\nK_{iji'j'mm'} \\;=\\; \\sum_{l} A_{ijml}\\, A_{i'j'm'l} \\;=\\; 4 \\sum_{l} \\Phi_{ijml}\\, \\Phi_{i'j'm'l}.\n$$\n\nEach $Q^{(ab)}$ is positive semidefinite (a sum of squares), and the contracted tensor $K$ is precomputed in the reference implementation (`octonion.py::build_K_tensor`). Because $G_2 = \\mathrm{Aut}(\\mathbb{O})$ preserves $\\phi$, hence $\\Phi$ and $A$, the covariance is manifest at the level of this formula:\n\n$$\nM_{ab}(gU;\\, gH) \\;=\\; M_{ab}(U;\\, H) \\qquad \\text{for all } g \\in G_2,\n$$\n\nand with $H$ fixed the residual symmetry is the stabilizer $\\mathrm{Stab}_{G_2}(H) \\cong SU(3)$. Any algebraic attack on the sum-rule conjecture (§5) should proceed through the standard $\\varepsilon$–$\\phi$–$\\Phi$ contraction identities applied to $K$; we deliberately leave $K$ uncontracted here rather than quote those identities without independent verification.\n\n### 2.2 Fragility of hollowness\n\nHollowness is the load-bearing property, and it is *fragile*: it belongs to the exact algebra. Truncating octonion multiplication to its imaginary part — a natural-looking simplification, and one this project's companion machine-learning study made — destroys alternativity, produces a generic diagonal, and erases every result below. (That truncation initially produced a spurious \"refutation\" of the golden-ratio behavior; the episode is documented in the project log as a caution: structural claims about an algebra must be tested with the exact algebra.)\n\n## 3. The n = 3 theorem: golden rigidity\n\n**Lemma 2 (sum rule).** *A real symmetric $3\\times3$ hollow matrix with nonnegative entries has singular values obeying $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$.*\n\n*Proof.* Perron–Frobenius for the nonnegative $M$ gives $\\lambda_1 = \\rho(M) \\geq |\\lambda_i|$. If $\\lambda_2 > 0$, tracelessness gives $|\\lambda_3| = \\lambda_1 + \\lambda_2 > \\rho(M)$, a contradiction; so $\\lambda_2, \\lambda_3 \\leq 0$ and $s_2 + s_3 = -(\\lambda_2 + \\lambda_3) = \\lambda_1 = s_1$. $\\square$\n\nThe sign structure is a special case of Charles–Farber–Johnson–Kennedy-Shaffer (SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl. 34, 2013), who show hollow symmetric nonnegative $n \\times n$ matrices have between $2$ and $n-1$ nonpositive eigenvalues; at $n = 3$ this forces exactly two. Our contribution is the octonionic application:\n\n**Theorem 1 (Golden Rigidity for n = 3).** *At every frame and every vacuum, the singular values of $M(U;H)$ ($n=3$) satisfy $s_1 = s_2 + s_3$. If the normalized spectrum is geometric, $(1, x, x^2)$, then $1 = x + x^2$ — the defining equation of the golden ratio — so $x = \\varphi^{-1} = 0.618034\\ldots$, uniquely.*\n\n> **Corollary 1 (exact Froggatt–Nielsen obstruction).** ***No frame and no vacuum yield a geometric spectrum at any base $x \\neq \\varphi^{-1}$; in particular Cabibbo textures ($x + x^2 \\approx 0.053 \\neq 1$) are excluded identically, and so is every strongly hierarchical texture $(1, \\epsilon, \\epsilon')$ with $\\epsilon + \\epsilon' < 1$. Conversely, the operator carries a rigid parameter-free signature: in the sum-rule normalization, $m_1 = m_2 + m_3$.***\n\n**Uniqueness is one-directional, and should not be overread.** The golden spectrum is the unique *geometric* spectrum, not the unique spectrum: on the sum-rule surface $s_2 + s_3 = s_1$ the normalized spectra $(1, r, 1-r)$ form a one-parameter family, and the original random scan realized $r = s_2/s_1$ across essentially its full admissible range $[0.5006,\\, 0.9994]$. The theorem collapses the geometric *locus* to a point; it does not collapse the operator's spectral range. (Consistently, the frame moduli here are higher-dimensional than the one-dimensional spectral family, so non-geometric spectra are generic and the golden point is a measure-zero target that optimization nevertheless reaches exactly.)\n\nVerification: sum-rule deviation $\\leq 6.5 \\times 10^{-16}$ over 2000 random Stiefel frames; $\\sim 10^{-7}$ over 300 non-orthonormal frames with random vacua. The theorem retroactively explains every feature of the original scans — the clustering of incidentally-geometric random frames at base $0.6181 \\pm 0.004$, the zero optimization residual at $\\varphi^{-1}$, and the $\\mathcal{O}(10^{-1})$ floors at all other prescribed bases.\n\n## 4. The k-bonacci family: n = 4 to 7\n\nFor $n \\geq 4$ the matrix facts weaken: hollow symmetric nonnegative matrices with only two nonpositive eigenvalues exist for every $n \\geq 4$ (CFJK), and for those the sum rule fails. Whether it survives is a question about the *image* of the octonionic map, not about hollow matrices in general. Empirically it survives everywhere:\n\n**Observation 1 (universal sum rule).** *Over 5,000–20,000 random frames per size, $n = 4, 5, 6, 7$: $\\max_U \\big| s_1 - \\sum_{i\\geq2} s_i \\big| / s_1 \\;\\leq\\; 1.2 \\times 10^{-15}$, and no sampled frame has a positive subdominant eigenvalue.*\n\nGranting the sum rule, a geometric ladder $(1, x, \\ldots, x^{n-1})$ must satisfy $1 = x + x^2 + \\cdots + x^{n-1}$, i.e. $x = 1/T_{n-1}$ with $T_k$ the k-bonacci constant (the root in $(1,2)$ of $t^k = t^{k-1} + \\cdots + 1$). Gradient searches for self-similar spectra — objectives written purely as $s_{i+1}^2 = s_i s_{i+2}$, never referencing any k-bonacci number — find:\n\n| $n$ | constant | predicted base $1/T_{n-1}$ | achieved base | ladder residual | sum-rule violation (max) | starts | epistemic status |\n|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|\n| 3 | golden | 0.6180340 | 0.6180340 | $0$ | $6.5 \\times 10^{-16}$ | — | **theorem** |\n| 4 | tribonacci | 0.5436890 | 0.5436890 | $< 10^{-28}$ (typ.) | $9.9 \\times 10^{-16}$ | 24/24 | numerically exact |\n| 5 | tetranacci | 0.5187901 | 0.5187901 | $3 \\times 10^{-32}$ | $9.3 \\times 10^{-16}$ | 8/8 | numerically exact |\n| 6 | pentanacci | 0.5086604 | 0.5086604 | $1 \\times 10^{-30}$ | $1.0 \\times 10^{-15}$ | 8/8 | numerically exact |\n| 7 | hexanacci | 0.5041383 | 0.5048538 | $1.5 \\times 10^{-8}$ (stall) | $8.7 \\times 10^{-16}$ | 0/28 | numerically excluded |\n\nThe rows do not share epistemic status: only $n = 3$ is proved; $n = 4$–$6$ are numerical realizations at machine precision (a proof of attainment is open); $n = 7$ is a numerical exclusion whose first-order structure is analyzed below.\n\n![Figure 1: (a) the k-bonacci base family with realized values; (b) the realized geometric ladders on a log scale — self-similarity appears as straight lines.](ladder_figure.png)\n\n**Observation 2 (realization, $n \\leq 6$).** *The octonion associator realizes the geometric ladder exactly at $x = 1/T_{n-1}$ for $n = 4, 5, 6$, and random-start gradient flows toward self-similarity converge to it with high reliability.*\n\n**Observation 3 (the $n = 7$ near-miss).** *At $n = 7$ — where the frame is a full orthonormal basis of $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ and the effective moduli collapse to $O(7)$ modulo the 14-dimensional $G_2$ automorphism action — 28 random starts under two barrier configurations stall at residual $\\sim 1.5 \\times 10^{-8}$, ten orders above the machine-zero convergence obtained with identical machinery at $n \\leq 6$. Achieved bases cluster at $0.5049$–$0.5054$, systematically $\\sim 9 \\times 10^{-4}$ above hexanacci, with the deviation concentrated in the two smallest rungs, while the sum rule continues to hold at $10^{-16}$ on every solution. We read this as evidence that the exact hexanacci ladder is not realizable: the octonionic image approaches the ladder locus to within $\\sim 10^{-4}$ per rung and appears to miss it.*\n\n## 5. Open problems\n\n**Conjecture (universal sum rule).** For all $n \\leq 7$ and all $u_1, \\ldots, u_n, H \\in \\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$, the singular values of $M(U;H)$ satisfy $s_1 = \\sum_{i \\geq 2} s_i$; equivalently, the octonionic image lies in the extreme stratum (exactly one positive eigenvalue) of hollow symmetric nonnegative matrices.\n\nThis is *not* a matrix-theoretic fact for $n \\geq 4$; a proof should exploit the $G_2$-invariant structure of the associator — e.g., its expression through the fundamental 3-form $\\phi$ and its Hodge dual [7] — rather than entrywise arguments. A positive resolution would classify the stratum of hollow nonnegative matrices realized by octonions, which seems independently interesting.\n\n**Problem (hexanacci non-realizability).** Prove or disprove: no orthonormal 7-frame of $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ gives $M(U; H)$ a geometric singular spectrum. The moduli reduction to $O(7)/G_2$ (dimension $21 - 14 = 7$) against the $5$ ladder constraints suggests a dimension count is *not* the obstruction, making the observed near-miss more curious, not less. A first-order (Jacobian) analysis sharpens the problem: at three independently converged stall points, $\\|J^\\top c\\| \\sim 10^{-8}$ (true critical points), the constraint Jacobian is effectively rank $4$ of $5$ ($\\sigma_5/\\sigma_1 \\approx 10^{-3}$), and the residual aligns with the collapsed direction to $|\\cos| = 1.0000$, with an identical residual signature across seeds — four of the five ladder conditions are satisfiable, and the fifth is blocked to first order on what appears to be a single canonical critical manifold. The analytic question is thus concrete: identify that manifold and show the fifth constraint's differential vanishes along it identically (code: `jacobian_test_n7.py`).\n\n**Question (interpolation).** The realized bases decrease monotonically toward $1/2$ (the $k \\to \\infty$ limit of $1/T_k$). Does the family's terminal misbehavior at $n = 7$ reflect the exhaustion of $\\mathrm{Im}(\\mathbb{O})$ — i.e., is the k-bonacci realization a strictly sub-maximal-frame phenomenon in any alternative algebra?\n\n## 6. Methods\n\nAll computations use the exact octonion algebra (Fano-plane structure constants with scalar parts retained; the associator tensor $B_{ijk} = [e_i, e_j, e_7]_k$ is precomputed exactly, making $M$ a bilinear `einsum` in the frame — the associator is trilinear, so no approximation is involved). Frames are parametrized by unconstrained matrices mapped to Stiefel frames by QR; searches use Adam (learning rates 0.02–0.03, up to 15,000 steps, float64) on the scale-free self-similarity objective $\\sum_i (s_{i+1}^2 - s_i s_{i+2})^2 / s_1^4$ with a small-rung barrier set *below* the target ladder's smallest rung (an earlier barrier of $0.02$ silently excluded the hexanacci target, whose smallest rung is $0.0163$ — the kind of guard-rail error worth documenting). Sum-rule scans use 5,000–20,000 frames per size. Everything runs on CPU in minutes; code: `tribonacci_test.py`, `mechanism_test.py` (tensor construction with built-in sum-rule self-check), and the original `fn_ladder_scan.py`.\n\n## 7. Relation to other golden-ratio phenomena\n\nGolden ratios arise in $E_8$-adjacent settings (folding to $H_4$; the Ising-chain $E_8$ spectrum with $m_2/m_1 = \\varphi$) and pervade quasicrystal geometry. The mechanism here is unrelated and elementary: antisymmetry makes the matrix hollow, nonnegativity plus tracelessness pin the spectrum's sign pattern, and self-similarity then has a unique fixed point — $1 = x + \\cdots + x^{n-1}$. The k-bonacci constants enter through their defining polynomials, not through any lattice or root system. We flag the coincidence to prevent, rather than to encourage, deeper numerology.\n\n## References\n\n1. J. C. Baez, *The octonions*, Bull. Amer. Math. Soc. **39** (2002) 145–205.\n2. R. D. Schafer, *An Introduction to Nonassociative Algebras*, Academic Press, 1966.\n3. Z. B. Charles, M. Farber, C. R. Johnson, L. Kennedy-Shaffer, *Nonpositive eigenvalues of hollow, symmetric, nonnegative matrices*, SIAM J. Matrix Anal. Appl. **34** (2013) 1384–1400.\n4. C. D. Froggatt, H. B. Nielsen, *Hierarchy of quark masses, Cabibbo angles and CP violation*, Nucl. Phys. B **147** (1979) 277–298.\n5. M. Günaydin, F. Gürsey, *Quark structure and octonions*, J. Math. Phys. **14** (1973) 1651–1667.\n6. R. Coldea et al., *Quantum criticality in an Ising chain: experimental evidence for emergent E8 symmetry*, Science **327** (2010) 177–180.\n7. R. Harvey, H. B. Lawson, *Calibrated geometries*, Acta Math. **148** (1982) 47–157.
